<a id="paper-2604.28026"></a>
### [Order by disorder up to arbitrarily high temperature](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28026v1)

**Authors:** Ravish Mehta  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28026v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.28026_figures/2604.28026_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 1: A configuration with two contours γ1 and γ2 with the boundary Bpωq denoted by the dark grey region and the patterned regions representing boundaries of the contours. The outer boundary has the phase η1 and the interior boundary has the same phase as that of the interior components along which they are drawn.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper provides a rigorous mathematical proof that certain classical lattice models can exhibit long-range order at arbitrarily high temperatures. This 'order by disorder' phenomenon occurs because entropy, rather than energy minimization, selects specific checkerboard configurations in the high-temperature limit.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Proving the existence of long-range checkerboard order in a class of classical lattice models at arbitrarily high temperatures via an entropic mechanism.

**Main result.** The author proves that a class of classical lattice models exhibits long-range checkerboard order in the high-temperature limit (beta -> 0), where the order is driven by entropy rather than energy minimization.

**Method.** The proof utilizes Pirogov-Sinai theory, cluster expansion, and a Peierls-type bound on contour surface energy to demonstrate phase coexistence.

**Model / system.** A classical lattice model on a hypercubic lattice Z^d (d >= 2) with unbounded occupation numbers (bosons) and a nearest-neighbor interaction function f(n_x, n_y) satisfying specific symmetry and growth conditions.

**Key observables.** Difference between the Gibbs measure of occupation labels and the reference checkerboard configurations; bulk free energy density.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Inverse temperature (beta -> 0 limit), dimension (d >= 2), and the growth exponent (alpha) of the level-set counting function.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The interaction function must satisfy four structural conditions (symmetry, vanishing on empty sites, strict penalty on occupied pairs, and specific growth); the analysis assumes a large-volume limit.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates a configuration with two contours, showing the boundary and the patterned regions representing the boundaries of the contours.

**Paper structure.** The paper establishes the model and its interaction properties, develops a polymer representation via cluster decomposition, applies Pirogov-Sinai theory to bound contour weights, and concludes with a proof of phase coexistence and uniform convergence to the checkerboard state.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We prove that a class of classical lattice models on $\mathbb{Z}^d$ ($d \geq 2$) with on-site space $\mathbb{N}_0$ exhibits long-range checkerboard order at sufficiently high temperature. The model has a nearest-neighbour interaction $f : \mathbb{N}_0 \times \mathbb{N}_0 \to [0,\infty)$ satisfying four structural conditions, subsuming the recently introduced power-law model of Han--Huang--Komargodski--Lucas--Popov (arXiv:2503.22789) as a special case. The ordering mechanism is purely entropic: the checkerboard configurations are not energy minimisers, but are selected by the partial trace over occupation numbers in the $β\to 0$ limit. The proof uses Pirogov--Sinai theory and the key input is a Peierls bound.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27087"></a>
### [Oscillators from non-semisimple walled Brauer algebras](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27087v1)

**Authors:** Sanjaye Ramgoolam, Michał Studziński  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27087v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** The paper provides a new method to calculate representation dimensions for walled Brauer algebras in non-semisimple regimes using modified Bratteli diagrams. It reveals a surprising connection between these algebraic dimension corrections and the partition functions of simple harmonic oscillators. This has implications for constructing matrix invariants in gauge theory and quantum information theory.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper addresses the representation theory of non-semisimple walled Brauer algebras B_N(m,n) in the regime where N < m + n, specifically how to compute dimension modifications in this regime.

**Main result.** The authors introduce restricted Bratteli diagrams to systematically compute dimension corrections and show that the resulting generating functions are governed by the partition function of an infinite tower of simple harmonic oscillators.

**Method.** The authors utilize a modification of standard Bratteli diagrams (restricted Bratteli diagrams) to track representation-theoretic data from the stable regime to the non-semisimple regime.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on walled Brauer algebras B_N(m,n) acting on mixed tensor spaces V_N^{tensor m} \otimes \overline{V}_N^{tensor n}, which are relevant to Schur-Weyl duality for unitary groups U(N).

**Key observables.** Representation dimensions and the partition function of the resulting oscillator system.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The regime N < m + n, specifically the case N = m + n - l where l is small compared to m and n.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis focuses on the stability property of restricted diagrams in the regime where the deviation from the stable regime (l) is small.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of non-semisimple walled Brauer algebras, presents the construction of restricted Bratteli diagrams, demonstrates a stability property for small l, identifies the connection to harmonic oscillator partition functions, and discusses applications to gauge theory and quantum information.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The walled Brauer algebras $B_N(m,n)$ govern Schur--Weyl duality for unitary groups $U(N)$ acting on mixed tensor spaces $V_N^{\otimes m}\otimes \overline{V}_N^{\otimes n}$ and play an important role in applications ranging from AdS/CFT to quantum information theory. In the stable regime $N\ge m+n$ the algebra is semisimple and its representation theory is well understood. For $N<m+n$, however, $B_N(m,n)$ becomes non-semisimple. The representation of the algebra on tensor space has a non-trivial kernel and the corresponding quotient algebra is semisimple, with representation dimensions differing from those in the stable regime.   We introduce \emph{restricted Bratteli diagrams}, obtained by modifying the standard Bratteli diagrams for $B_N(m,n)$. This construction provides a systematic way to use representation-theoretic data from the stable regime to compute the dimension modifications arising in the non-semisimple regime. In the regime $N=m+n-l$, with $l$ small compared to $m,n$, we show that the restricted diagrams exhibit a stability property and enable an efficient counting of the paths responsible for these dimension corrections.   Remarkably, the resulting generating functions are governed by the partition function of an infinite tower of simple harmonic oscillators. We briefly discuss implications for the construction of orthogonal bases of matrix invariants in gauge theory and related applications in quantum information theory.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27522"></a>
### [Pauli equation in spaces of constant curvature and extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27522v1)

**Authors:** Abdaljalel E. Alizzi, Zurab K. Silagadze  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27522v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** The paper examines the application of the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method to the Pauli equation in curved spaces. It concludes that the method is likely unreliable for this purpose because the required conditions for polynomial solutions cannot be satisfied. This highlights a fundamental difficulty in solving the Heun equation in this context.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the validity of applying the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method to solve the radial Heun equation arising from the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation in curved spaces.

**Main result.** The authors find that the necessary conditions for the existence of polynomial solutions in the Heun equation cannot be met, suggesting that the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method has limited utility for these specific quantum mechanical problems.

**Method.** The study utilizes the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method applied to the radial equation derived from the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation.

**Model / system.** The system consists of a non-relativistic particle (the Pauli equation limit) in spaces of constant curvature subject to a Coulomb potential.

**Key observables.** Energy spectrum and quantization conditions.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Curvature of the space and the Coulomb potential strength.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation can be treated via the Heun equation framework.

**Paper structure.** The paper presents an application of a mathematical method to a physical problem, analyzes the resulting energy spectrum and quantization conditions, and concludes with a critique of the method's reliability based on the impossibility of meeting polynomial solution conditions.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We apply the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method to the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation with a Coulomb potential in spaces of constant curvature. In this case, the radial equation reduces to the Heun equation, and the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method easily yields a quantization condition which leads to necessary condition under which the resulting Heun equation can have polynomial solutions. The energy spectrum implied by the quantization condition is virtually identical to the spectrum of a spinless particle obtained using the Schrödinger equation, except for the absence of the ``geometric potential", confirming the non-commutativity of the naive non-relativistic limit with the ``squaring" of the Dirac equation, first discovered on curved surfaces. However, the necessary conditions for the existence of polynomial solutions cannot be met, and this fact undermines the reliability of the results obtained. This circumstance forces us to conclude that the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method has limited, if any, value when considering similar problems in quantum mechanics.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

### [Q3SAT-GPT: A Generative Model for Discovering Quantum Circuits for the 3-SAT Problem](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27324v1)

**Authors:** Pratim Ugale, Ilya Tyagin, Karunya Shirali, Kien X. Nguyen, Ilya Safro

**Summary.** This paper introduces Q3SAT-GPT, a generative AI model that learns to design quantum circuits for solving 3-SAT problems. By training on circuits produced by a new adaptive algorithm (MosaicADAPT-QAOA), the model can bypass expensive optimization steps and propose high-quality solutions in a single step. This approach offers a scalable route toward discovering efficient quantum algorithms for combinatorial optimization.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The challenge of efficiently discovering high-quality, low-depth quantum circuits for the Max-E3-SAT combinatorial optimization problem without the heavy computational cost of iterative variational optimization.

**Main result.** The Q3SAT-GPT generative model can predict optimized quantum circuits in a single forward pass with high approximation ratios and significantly faster amortized inference time compared to classical optimization-based adaptive methods.

**Method.** A generative transformer-based architecture (Q3SAT-GPT) is trained using data generated by a new adaptive strategy called MosaicADAPT-QAOA, which uses a Maximum Weight Independent Set approach to select multiple disjoint operators per layer.

**Model / system.** The problem involves Max-E3-SAT instances (Uniform Random and Balanced) mapped to a cost Hamiltonian using a Higher-Order Unconstrained Binary Optimization (HUBO) formulation with Pauli-Z operators.

**Key observables.** Approximation Ratio (AR), Circuit Error Rate (ER), and circuit depth.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Phase transition ratio (alpha), number of variables (n), and the initial gamma parameter (gamma_0).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The performance of the generative model is bounded by the quality of the training data produced by the MosaicADTP-QAOA algorithm; the focus is limited to the Max-E3-SAT problem class.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the conflict in greedy operator selection; Figure 2 illustrates an incompatibility graph; Figure 3 details the model pipeline; Figure 4 compares energy convergence; Figure 5 shows gradient norms; Figure 6 shows operator evolution; Figure 7 compares predicted vs. optimized parameters.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of circuit discovery, presents the MosaicADAPT-QAOA adaptive strategy, describes the Q3SAT-GPT generative architecture and training pipeline, evaluates performance against classical and quantum baselines, and discusses limitations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

This work introduces Q3SAT-GPT, a generative model for discovering quantum circuits for the Max-E3-SAT problem. Our method learns from high-performing QAOA-style ansätze to directly generate candidate circuits. To create high-quality supervision, we also introduce Mosaic Adaptive QAOA (MosaicADAPT-QAOA), an adaptive strategy for constructing low-depth QAOA circuits by selecting subsets of mixer operators in each step, rather than inserting operators sequentially. The resulting circuits serve as training data for the generative model, allowing it to learn effective circuit design patterns while eliminating the need for costly variational optimization at inference time. Experiments show that our framework attains strong solution quality with shallow circuits and scales significantly better than both our adaptive construction procedure and conventional variational baselines. Our results establish generative modeling as a high-performance route toward the scalable discovery of quantum optimization circuits, demonstrating that these models can effectively internalize circuit logic while providing a foundation for future, instance-aware inductive biases. Reproducibility: The source code is available at https://github.com/pratimugale/Q3SAT-GPT.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27632"></a>
### [Quantum Scalar Spin Chirality in Coplanar Kagome Antiferromagnets](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27632v1)

**Authors:** Nanse Esaki, Gyungchoon Go, Se Kwon Kim  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27632v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** This paper shows that even in magnets where spins are arranged in a plane, quantum fluctuations can create a sense of 'handedness' or scalar spin chirality. This effect is significant because the magnitude of these fluctuations can be as large as the static chirality found in non-coplanar magnets.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating whether quantum fluctuations can generate scalar spin chirality in antiferromagnets that possess a coplanar classical ground state.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that quantum fluctuations can induce scalar spin chirality at zero temperature in coplanar kagome antiferromagnets, provided certain symmetry-breaking conditions are met, with fluctuations increasing at finite temperatures.

**Method.** Theoretical analysis of quantum fluctuations and the effective Hamiltonian describing fluctuations in a kagome antiferromagnet.

**Model / system.** A kagome antiferromagnet with coplanar ordered spin configurations.

**Key observables.** Scalar spin chirality and its fluctuations.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Zero temperature and finite temperature (thermally excited magnons); magnetic point group of the classical ground state.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The presence of scalar spin chirality depends on the breaking of an effective time-reversal-like antiunitary symmetry in the fluctuation Hamiltonian.

**Paper structure.** The paper presents a theoretical demonstration of quantum-induced scalar spin chirality, discusses the symmetry requirements for its emergence in coplanar kagome systems, and analyzes the temperature dependence of these fluctuations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We theoretically demonstrate that quantum fluctuations inherent to antiferromagnets can generate scalar spin chirality at zero temperature even in coplanar ordered magnets. In a kagome antiferromagnet with coplanar ground-state spin configurations, the quantum-fluctuation-induced scalar spin chirality is shown to arise at zero temperature when an effective time-reversal-like antiunitary symmetry is broken in the Hamiltonian describing fluctuations, and a magnetic point group of the classical ground state allows for its presence. The scalar spin chirality fluctuations are shown to grow further with increasing temperature by thermally excited magnons. These scalar spin chirality fluctuations can reach a magnitude comparable to the static one predicted for noncoplanar spin structures, highlighting their physical implications in coplanar spin systems.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27226"></a>
### [Ratio-Dependent Contrarian Activation in Opinion Dynamics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27226v1)

**Authors:** Serge Galam  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27226v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">

Outside the colored area in the white area only the fixed point pc = 1</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Figure 3: The complete landscape of the dynamics including alternating regimes. Four domains are shown as a function of c3,0 and c2,1. The domains are separated by the lines c3,0 = 1</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Figure 4: Four different regimes produced by the update Equation (11) with a tipping point coupled to two attractors, a single attractor, an alternating single attractor and an alternating tipping point coupled to two alternating attractors, for respectively (c3,0 = 0.05, c2,1 = 0.15), (c3,0 = 0.12, c2,1 = 0.22), (c3,0 = 0.88, c2,1 = 0.78), (c3,0 = 0.95, c2,1 = 0.85).</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> Figure 5: Various main stages of the variation p ¯ A in red and p ¯B in blue as a function of c2,1 for the series of given values c3,0 = 0, 0.01, 0.17, 0.3, 0.35, 0.99. The fixed point pc = 1</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper extends the Galam Majority Model by making contrarian behavior dependent on the local ratio of opinions in a group. It reveals a complex landscape of dynamics, showing how specific contrarian strategies can either reinforce a majority or drive a system toward a 50/50 polarized state.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how opinion dynamics change when the activation of contrarians depends on the local majority/minority ratio rather than being a uniform probability.

**Main result.** The study identifies a two-dimensional landscape of four distinct dynamical domains, including regimes of majority/minority consensus, polarization (50/50 attractor), and alternating dynamics.

**Method.** Analytical derivation of update equations for the Galam Majority Model, followed by fixed point and stability analysis using derivatives and Taylor expansion.

**Model / system.** An extension of the Galam Majority Model (GMM) involving discussion groups of size 3 with agents acting as conformists or ratio-dependent contrarians.

**Key observables.** Proportion of agents with opinion A (p_n), fixed points (p_c), and stability of attractors.

**Important parameters / regimes.** c_3,0 (contrarian probability in unanimous groups), c_2,1 (contrarian probability in 2:1 groups), and the uniform limit c.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The model is restricted to group sizes of 3 and assumes the validity of the dynamics for contrarian probabilities between 0 and 1.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a phase diagram of the dynamical domains; Figure 5 illustrates the variation of opinion levels as a function of c_2,1 for various fixed c_3,0.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of mixed contrarians, defines the extended Galam Majority Model, provides the analytical derivation of update equations, performs fixed point and stability analysis to map the dynamical landscape, and discusses strategic implications.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

I study the impact of mixed contrarians on the opinion dynamics of an heterogenous population with conformists using Galam Majority Model. Activation of contrarians is a function of the ratio majority/minority in the local groups of discussion. Restricting the group size to 3, two types of contrarians are included in respective proportions $c_{3,0}$ for configurations with ratio 3 to 0 and $c_{2,1}$ for ratio 2 to 1. I then derive the explicit update Equation and obtained analytically the fixed points, their stability, and the resulting full two-dimensional landscape of the dynamics of opinion. Setting $c_{3,0} =c_{2,1} = c$ recovers the original results obtained with uniform contrarians. The findings allow for considering a wide spectrum of new disruptive strategies to secure either a majority/minority ending ensuring the opinion having the larger initial support to win, or a single attractor dynamics at fifty/fifty, which implies a random winner regardless of initial supports.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27738"></a>
### [Sampling two-dimensional spin systems with transformers](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27738v1)

**Authors:** Piotr Białas, Piotr Korcyl, Tomasz Stebel, Adam Stefański, Dawid Zapolski  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** disordered systems and neural networks · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27738v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** The authors present an efficient transformer-based neural sampler for 2D classical spin systems by generating groups of spins rather than single spins. This method significantly outperforms previous neural samplers in terms of Effective Sample Size, even when applied to larger system sizes and disordered models like the Edwards-Anderson model.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The computational inefficiency of using transformer architectures for sampling classical spin systems compared to dense or convolutional neural networks.

**Main result.** A novel transformer-based sampler that generates groups of spins simultaneously and uses approximated probabilities, achieving an Effective Sample Size 20 times larger than previous state-of-the-art samplers for the 128x128 Ising model at critical temperature.

**Method.** An autoregressive transformer-based approach that employs group-based spin generation and a model of approximated probabilities to improve sampling efficiency.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on two-dimensional classical spin systems, specifically the Ising model and the 2D Edwards-Anderson spin glass model.

**Key observables.** Effective Sample Size (ESS)

**Important parameters / regimes.** System sizes up to 180x180 for the Ising model and 64x64 for the Edwards-Anderson model; critical temperature for the Ising model.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces a new transformer-based sampling architecture, describes the group-generation and probability approximation techniques, and evaluates performance on the Ising and Edwards-Anderson models.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Autoregressive Neural Networks based on dense or convolutional layers have recently been shown to be a viable strategy for generating classical spin systems. Unlike these methods, sampling with transformers is commonly considered to be computationally inefficient. In this work, we propose a novel approach to transformer-based neural samplers in which we generate not a single spin per step but groups of spins. As an additional improvement, we construct a model of approximated probabilities, further improving the efficiency of the algorithm. Despite our approach being computationally heavier than dense networks or CNN-based approaches, we were able to sample larger systems of up to $180 \times 180$ spins in case of the Ising model. The Effective Sample Size of our sampler is $\sim 20$ times larger than that of the previous state-of-the-art neural sampler when trained for the $128 \times 128$ Ising model at critical temperature. Finally, we also test our algorithm on the 2D Edwards-Anderson model, where we train $64\times 64$ spin systems.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.28089"></a>
### [Source-independent quantum key distribution without pre-sending entanglement](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28089v1)

**Authors:** Rong-Zheng Liu, Hua-Lei Yin  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28089v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** The paper introduces a source-independent QKD protocol that protects against all source-side side-channel attacks without requiring pre-distributed entanglement. It demonstrates that this approach can double the transmission distance and benefits significantly from using non-classical light sources.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant to quantum optics and quantum information as it addresses fundamental security vulnerabilities in photonic quantum communication and explores the advantages of non-classical light.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The vulnerability of prepare-and-measure QKD protocols to side-channel attacks targeting the light source, even when using perfect single-photon sources or passive schemes.

**Main result.** A new source-independent (SI) QKD protocol that eliminates all known and unknown source-side attacks without the need for pre-sending entanglement, while doubling transmission distance.

**Method.** The authors propose a source-independent protocol and provide a theoretical analysis comparing the performance of conventional lasers versus non-classical light sources.

**Model / system.** The protocol involves quantum light sources, specifically comparing conventional laser-based decoy-state methods with non-classical light sources in a QKD network setup.

**Important parameters / regimes.** transmission distance, source imperfection, non-classicality of the light source

**Assumptions / limitations.** The protocol assumes the ability to utilize non-classical light sources and aims to be robust against any source-side side-channel attacks.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of source-side attacks in BB84, proposes a new SI-QKD protocol, and provides theoretical analysis regarding distance and source types.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum key distribution (QKD) theoretically offers information-theoretic security. The prevailing approach is the prepare-and-measure BB84 protocol, which implements QKD using conventional laser rather than single-photon source via the decoy-state method. However, side-channel attacks targeting sources severely threaten system security. Despite extensive efforts, including fully passive scheme, this vulnerability persists even with perfect single-photon source. Here, we propose a source-independent (SI) QKD protocol that resolves all known and unknown source-side attacks without pre-sending entanglement source. Aligning with advances in quantum light sources, our protocol simultaneously doubles the transmission distance while remaining robustness against imperfection of source. Theoretical analysis shows that non-classical light source provides practical security advantages unattainable with conventional laser.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27136"></a>
### [Stepping up enhanced rate calculations with EATR-flooding](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27136v1)

**Authors:** Nicodemo Mazzaferro, Willmor J Pena Ccoa, Pilar Cossio, Glen M. Hocky  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27136v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** The paper presents EATR-flooding, a new method for calculating rate constants in molecular simulations using stepped-up biasing potentials. This approach extends the EATR method to quasi-static sampling schemes like OPES, making it more versatile and easier to implement. It also introduces an internal check for over-biasing and simplifies the dependence of the CV-quality factor.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The original EATR method for computing rate constants requires a time-dependent bias, which limits its use in quasi-static biasing schemes like OPES or flooding.

**Main result.** The authors introduce EATR-flooding, a generalization that uses stepped-up biasing strengths across multiple simulations to estimate rates, providing an internal check for over-biasing and a more stable CV-quality factor.

**Method.** The method replaces time-dependent biasing with a series of simulations with increasing biasing potential strengths (stepping up) and utilizes a learned CV-quality factor gamma.

**Model / system.** The method is demonstrated on a coarse-grained protein system and a fully atomistic cavity-ligand model.

**Key observables.** Rate constants of slow biomolecular processes and the CV-quality factor gamma.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The biasing potential strength and the CV-quality factor gamma.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The method assumes the applicability of the EATR framework to quasi-static biasing schemes and relies on the accuracy of the learned quality factor.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the limitation of the original EATR, presents the new EATR-flooding approach, describes the implementation as an open-source Python library, and validates the method using protein and cavity-ligand models.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Several recent methods have shown that it is possible to compute rate constants of very slow biomolecular processes using simulations where a time-dependent bias is added along one or several collective variables (CVs). We previously reported the exponential average time-dependent rate (EATR) method, which can improve upon these approaches by accounting for how efficiently the external biasing potential modifies the observed rate using a learned CV-quality factor $γ$. This results in more accurate rate estimates using the same data when biasing a suboptimal coordinate. However, as formulated EATR depended on the biasing potential varying over time to properly determine the biasing efficiency, which limits the method's applicability to quasi-static biasing schemes such as ``flooding'' or on-the-fly probability enhanced sampling (OPES). Here, we present the EATR-flooding approach, which generalizes our method by replacing the need for a time dependent bias by instead varying (stepping up) the strength of the biasing potential across multiple sets of simulations. We implement this approach as an open-source Python library, and demonstrate that this approach is accurate without substantial loss of efficiency compared to standard EATR for a coarse-grained protein system, and also show good performance on a fully atomistic cavity-ligand model. Two additional appealing features of EATR-flooding are an internal check for over-biasing and the fact that only a single $γ$ parameter is predicted for a given choice of CVs, as compared to our earlier results where $γ$ empirically depended on biasing rate. Finally, we believe EATR-flooding applies not only to OPES simulations but more generally to CV biasing enhanced sampling approaches, making it broadly useful.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27222"></a>
### [The Great Chicken-and-Egg of Chemistry: Bonding vs. Stability Revisited](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27222v1)

**Authors:** Cherif F. Matta  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27222v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27222_figures/2604.27222_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Fig. 1. Logical flow to chemical bonding descriptors starting from the of the Born–</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper challenges the common chemical practice of treating bonds as physical causes of stability, arguing instead that they are emergent descriptors of the underlying quantum state. By analyzing the molecular Hamiltonian, the author shows that bonding accompanies stability without being its fundamental driver. This reclassification helps resolve circular reasoning in chemical theory.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper addresses the logical fallacy in chemistry where chemical bonding and steric repulsion are incorrectly treated as fundamental causal agents of structural stability rather than derived descriptors of the quantum state.

**Main result.** The author demonstrates that bonding is a pattern within the quantum state that correlates with stability but does not constitute its cause, providing evidence through the H-H bonding paradox where local stabilization occurs in globally unstable structures.

**Method.** The paper employs a logical and philosophical analysis of the molecular Hamiltonian, utilizing topological frameworks like QTAIM, NCI, and the virial theorem to evaluate electron density properties.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on molecular systems (including proteins and hydrocarbons) described by the nonrelativistic molecular Hamiltonian under the Born-Oppenheimer approximation.

**Key observables.** Electron density, Laplacian of the electron density, bond paths, virial paths, and energy densities.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Stationary points on the potential energy hypersurface (minima and saddle points), and the local virial theorem.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The argument assumes the validity of the Born-Oppenheimer approximation and uses an interventionist definition of causality.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates the logical flow from the Born-Oppenheimer approximation to chemical descriptors, highlighting the fallacy of using derived descriptors as causes for structural stability.

**Paper structure.** The paper moves from the mathematical reality of the Hamiltonian to the identification of logical inversions in chemical language, uses case studies like H-H bonding to prove non-causality, and concludes with a philosophical defense of chemical autonomy.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The chemical bond is a central organizing concept in chemistry, yet it is absent from the molecular Hamiltonian and no "bond operator" exists. Bonding is therefore not a primitive physical entity but a derived descriptor emerging from the quantum state. The logical consequences of this observation are revisited. Statements such as "bonding stabilizes structure" when taken literally risk circular reasoning (petitio principii), whereby bonding is inferred from a stationary structure and then invoked as its cause. The same caution applies to concepts such as steric repulsion, which is also a derived descriptor. Bonding accompanies stable or metastable states and correlates with their properties without constituting their cause. Illustrative examples are drawn from QTAIM, non-covalent interaction (NCI) approach, protein structure, and hydrogen-hydrogen bonding. Causation, language, and the autonomy of chemistry are also briefly discussed. The aim is not at all to diminish the role of bonding, but to place it at the correct logical level, that is, as a powerful, state-dependent descriptor that organizes, classifies, and predicts chemical behavior without serving as its fundamental cause.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

### [The quantum group structure of long-range integrable deformations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27189v1)

**Authors:** Koen Schouten, Marius de Leeuw  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27189v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 9.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 10</figcaption>

</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper provides a new algebraic description of long-range integrable spin chains by showing they arise from a twist of the underlying quantum group. It demonstrates that this twisting leads to a non-associative structure where the Drinfeld associator encodes the long-range interactions. The work provides explicit tools, such as new algebraic charge densities, to study these deformed integrable models.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper aims to identify the underlying quantum group structure for long-range integrable deformations of homogeneous Yang-Baxter integrable spin chains.

**Main result.** The authors provide a quantum group-theoretical description showing that these deformations are obtained via a twist of the underlying algebraic structure, resulting in a non-associative algebra characterized by a Drinfeld associator.

**Method.** The study utilizes FRT-bialgebras, the quantum inverse scattering method, and deformation theory, specifically analyzing the twist mechanism and introducing 'algebraic charge densities' via derivatives of the R-matrix.

**Model / system.** The research focuses on quantum integrable spin chains, including the Heisenberg (XXX) model, Haldane-Shastry, and Inozemtsev chains, specifically looking at long-range deformations generated by local, boost, and bilocal operators.

**Key observables.** Conserved charges (local and algebraic), transfer matrix, Lax operators, R-matrices, and the Drinfeld associator.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The deformation parameter (analyzed to first order) and the spectral parameter.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The results are perturbative and limited to the first order in the deformation parameter; the R-matrix is assumed to be regular and unitary.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of long-range deformations, establishes the FRT-bialgebra framework, applies a twisting mechanism to describe the deformation, proves the existence of the Drinfeld associator, and provides explicit expressions for Lax operators and R-matrices.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum integrable spin chains are known to possess a large family of long-range deformations generated by the local, boost and bilocal operators. Although these deformations are well-understood on the level of the pairwise commuting charges, the underlying quantum group structures had not yet been recognised. In this paper, we provide a quantum group-theoretical description for the family of long-range deformations of arbitrary homogeneous Yang-Baxter integrable spin chains up to first order in the deformation parameter. In particular, we show that the deformations are obtained via a twist of the algebraic structure of the underlying quantum group. This twisting results in a generally non-associative algebra that has a non-trivial Drinfeld associator. The Drinfeld associator is then shown to encode the information about the long-range interaction terms for the integrable spin chain. Moreover, the deformed quantum group is shown to contain a large perturbatively associative substructure, thus ensuring the perturbative integrability of the long-range model. The deformed quantum group provides explicit expressions for the Lax operators and R-matrices of the long-range deformed models, which manifestly satisfy the RLL relation and the Yang-Baxter equation up to first order in the deformation parameter. In order to derive the results, we introduce algebra elements that we call the algebraic charge densities. As a side result, we provide a conjecture for the explicit expressions of the undeformed charge densities in terms of these algebra elements.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27746"></a>
### [The second altermagnet candidate in organic conductors: $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2$$m$-HOOCC$_6$H$_4$SO$_3$](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27746v1)

**Authors:** Kohei Tokura, Takato Masuta, Kazushi Aoyama, Hiroki Akutsu, Yasuhiro Nakazawa, Scott S. Turner  
**Type:** both · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27746v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. Frustration of spins on a triangular lattice.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> FIG. 2. (a) Crystal structure of κ-m-SBA, where disorders are omitted for clarity. (b) Structure of the κ-type donor arrangement.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> FIG. 3. χ-T plots of κ-m-SBA. The inset shows the expansion from 16-300 K.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> FIG. 4. M-H plots of κ-m-SBA.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> FIG. 5. The energy bands of κ-m-SBA.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The researchers synthesized a new organic conductor, kappa-m-SBA, and identified it as a rare candidate for altermagnetism. By combining experimental measurements with numerical simulations, they demonstrated that the material exhibits spin-split energy bands driven by its specific magnetic ordering. This provides a new platform for studying altermagnetic phenomena in organic molecular crystals.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The identification of a new candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors and explaining why the material kappa-m-SBA exhibits a canted antiferromagnetic transition instead of a spin liquid state.

**Main result.** The discovery of kappa-m-SBA as the second organic altermagnet candidate, demonstrating characteristic spin-splitting of energy bands due to the interplay of AFM order and anisotropic hopping.

**Method.** The study combines electrocrystallization synthesis, SQUID magnetometry, and four-probe resistivity measurements with first-principles (OpenMX) and tight-binding band calculations using a Hubbard model.

**Model / system.** The system is a kappa-type organic conductor, kappa-(BEDT-TTF)2m-HOOCC6H4SO3, characterized by a nearly equilateral triangular lattice and a Hubbard model Hamiltonian including intra-dimer and inter-dimer transfer integrals.

**Key observables.** Néel temperature (TN = 14 K), magnetic susceptibility, magnetization, electrical resistivity, spin-dependent band splitting, and the frustration parameter (t'/t).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Transfer integrals (t, t', tp, tq), Coulomb interaction (U = 0.54 eV), Mott gap (0.22 eV), and the frustration parameter (t'/t approx 1.01 or 0.80).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The canted antiferromagnetic structure is approximated as a collinear antiferromagnetic structure to evaluate lattice symmetry-driven altermagnetism.

**Figures summary.** Figure 5 shows the energy band dispersion in the AFM insulating phase demonstrating spin splitting; Figure S8 illustrates the crystal structure of the anionic layer.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces a new organic conductor, describes its synthesis and structural properties, presents magnetic and transport measurements, uses first-principles and tight-binding calculations to analyze the electronic and magnetic ground state, and concludes with the identification of altermagnetic signatures.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We have developed a novel BEDT-TTF-based organic conductor, $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2 m$-HOOCC$_6$H$_4$SO$_3$ ($κ$-$m$-SBA), and propose it as a candidate for altermagnet. Tight-binding band calculations of $κ$-$m$-SBA provide a $t'/t$ of 1.01 at 100 K, indicating that the spin structure is closely aligned to an equilateral triangle ($t'/t= 1$). While most $κ$-type BEDT-TTF-based salts become spin liquids due to the spin frustration caused by the triangular lattice, $κ$-$m$-SBA surprisingly shows a weak ferromagnetic transition at $T_\mathrm{N} = 14$ K due to a canted antiferromagnetic (AFM) spin structure. Until recently, $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2$Cu[N(CN)$_2$]Cl ($κ$-Cl) was the only $κ$-type organic conductor known to exhibit this order, and it is also recognized as the first candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors. This was theoretically predicted by Naka et al. in 2019, who demonstrated that $κ$-type organic conductors can be candidates for altermagnetism if they display such order. Consequently, $κ$-$m$-SBA can be considered the second candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors. Furthermore, numerical calculations demonstrate a characteristic of altermagnets in $κ$-$m$-SBA, namely spin splitting of energy bands.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27304"></a>
### [Topological phase transitions in twisted bilayer graphene/hBN from interlayer coupling and substrate potentials](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27304v1)

**Authors:** Huiwen Wang, Wei Jiang  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27304v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** This paper investigates how varying interlayer coupling and substrate potentials affects the topological properties of twisted bilayer graphene/hBN. It identifies new high-Chern number states and explains the mechanisms behind the resulting topological phase transitions. These findings help interpret experimental observations in moire materials.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study aims to provide a systematic understanding of how the combined influence of interlayer coupling and substrate potentials drives topological phase transitions in twisted bilayer graphene/hBN.

**Main result.** The authors map out Chern number phase diagrams revealing a rich topological landscape, including high-Chern number states (C = 3, 4, and 5), and identify the specific band-inversion mechanisms driving these transitions.

**Method.** A comprehensive theoretical study using a continuum model to vary material parameters and analyze the evolution of Berry curvature.

**Model / system.** Twisted bilayer graphene aligned with hexagonal boron nitride (TBG/hBN) described by a continuum model including interlayer hopping and hBN-induced potentials.

**Key observables.** Chern number, Berry curvature, and band-inversion mechanisms.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Interlayer hopping strengths (w0, w1), hBN-induced staggered potential, and the presence or absence of the hBN moire potential.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study relies on the validity of the continuum model for describing the moire physics in TBG/hBN.

**Paper structure.** The paper presents a systematic study of topological phase transitions by mapping phase diagrams across a parameter space and analyzing the underlying band-inversion mechanisms.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Twisted bilayer graphene aligned with hexagonal boron nitride (TBG/hBN) hosts rich topological and correlated quantum phases, such as (fractional) Chern insulators, whose character is dictated by the topology of the moiré flat band. This topology is highly sensitive to several material parameters in the continuum model, yet a systematic understanding of their combined influence has been lacking. Here, we present a comprehensive study of topological phase transitions in TBG/hBN by varying the interlayer hopping strengths ($w_0, w_1$) and hBN-induced staggered potential, both with and without the hBN moiré potential. We map out Chern number phase diagrams across a broad, experimentally relevant parameter space, revealing a progressive enrichment of the topological landscape including multiple high-Chern number ($C$ = 3, 4, and 5) states. Each transition is linked to distinct band-inversion mechanisms at generic $C_3$-symmetric k points, high-symmetry momenta, or parabolic touchings, clearly reflecting in the evolution of the Berry curvature. Our results offer theoretical insights that help interpret existing experimental observations, elucidate the mechanisms driving these topological phase transitions and facilitate the exploration of topological states in TBG/hBN and related moiré systems.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27256"></a>
### [Towards Accelerated SCF Workflows with Equivariant Density-Matrix Learning and Analytic Refinement](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27256v1)

**Authors:** Zuriel Y. Yescas-Ramos, Andrés Álvarez-García, Huziel E. Sauceda  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** numerical methods · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27256v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27256_figures/2604.27256_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. dm-PhiSNet model. (A) The PhiSNet-based backbone (gray box) builds blockwise AO 1-RDMs from molecular geometries R and atomic numbers Z, which are then refined by the analytic block (green box) to give the 1-RDM predictor. (B) Representation of the PhiSNet architecture. [25] (C) The AnalyticBlock is constructed by three sub-blocks to enforce physical consistency using the overlap matrix S: (i) trace rescaling, (ii) McWeeny purification cycle, and (iii) a final trace rescaling.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27256_figures/2604.27256_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> FIG. 2. Mean numbers of SCF iterations over 500 test configurations for all benchmarked systems. Results compare the performance of the 1-RDMs predicted by our model against the conventional SAD (atom), MINAO, and H¨uckel initial guesses. Magnitudes of the standard deviations (STD) are represented by vertical black lines on the frequency bars. Reductions with respect to the three averaged standard initial guesses are also shown.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2604.27256_figures/2604.27256_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> FIG. 3. (A) Distributions of single-point errors in total en- ergy ∆E (left axis) and force norms ∥∆F∥(right axis) com- puted directly from the predicted 1-RDM ˆP0, for ethanol (top panel) and NO− 3 (bottom panel). (B) Conceptual integration into MD: conventional SCF versus using ˆP0 either (i) directly for an SCF-free MD step (as a CP-style electronic initializer) or (ii) as a warm start for accelerated SCF refinement for BO- MD.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper introduces dm-PhiSNet, a machine learning model designed to accelerate quantum chemistry calculations by predicting high-quality initial density matrices. By enforcing physical constraints like idempotency and charge conservation, the model significantly reduces the number of iterations needed for SCF convergence and can even predict accurate forces in a single step.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Accelerating Self-Consistent Field (SCF) workflows in electronic-structure theory by generating physically admissible initial density matrix guesses.

**Main result.** The dm-PhiSNet model reduces SCF iteration steps by 49-81% and provides accurate one-shot total energies and Hellmann-Feynman forces without explicit force supervision.

**Method.** A two-stage training protocol using an equivariant PhiSNet backbone combined with a lightweight analytic refinement block that enforces physical constraints like electron-number conservation and generalized idempotency.

**Model / system.** The model predicts one-electron reduced density matrices (1-RDMs) in an atomic-orbital basis for closed-shell molecular systems including H2O, CH4, NH3, HF, ethanol, and NO3-.

**Key observables.** One-electron reduced density matrices (1-RDMs), total energies, Hellmann-Feynman atomic forces, and SCF iteration counts.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The work focuses on closed-shell systems and assumes the effectiveness of projecting learned 1-RDMs onto the admissible manifold at negligible computational cost.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 details the dm-PhiSNet architecture, including the equivariant backbone and the analytic refinement sub-blocks. Figure 2 shows the reduction in SCF iterations compared to standard initializations, and Figure 3 presents error distributions for energy and force norms.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the dm-PhiSNet architecture, describes the equivariant backbone and the analytic constraint enforcement, details the two-stage training protocol, presents benchmarks on molecular systems regarding SCF acceleration and one-shot accuracy, and discusses scalability and limitations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We present \textsc{dm-PhiSNet}, a physically constrained \textsc{PhiSNet}-based equivariant model that predicts one-electron reduced density matrices (1-RDMs) directly from molecular geometries in an atomic-orbital (AO) basis for accelerated self-consistent field (SCF) workflows. Training follows a two-stage schedule with progressively introduced physically motivated objectives, and the resulting predictions are refined by a lightweight analytic block. This block enforces electron-number conservation, drives the 1-RDM toward generalized idempotency in the AO metric, and regularizes the occupation spectrum of the Löwdin-orthogonalized density. Across six closed-shell systems -- H$_2$O, CH$_4$, NH$_3$, HF, ethanol, and NO$_3^-$ -- the refined 1-RDMs provide SCF initial guesses that substantially reduce iteration steps by 49--81\% relative to standard initializations. Beyond SCF acceleration, the learned 1-RDMs yield accurate one-shot total energies and Hellmann--Feynman atomic forces without force supervision, indicating that the model captures chemically meaningful electronic structure. These results demonstrate that combining equivariant learning with analytic constraint enforcement provides a simple, general route to solver-ready density-matrix initializations and accelerated SCF workflows.

</details>

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.28145"></a>
### [Strong coupling between quantized magnon modes in a YIG microstucture and microwaves in a superconducting resonator](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28145v1)

**Authors:** Seth W. Kurfman, Philipp Geyer, Anoop Kamalasanan, Karl Heimrich, Kwangyul Hu, Paul Tharnier, Frank Heyroth, Michael Flatté, Georg Schmidt  
**Type:** experiment · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28145v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **5/5** · 🔥 `QC/QI experiment` **4/5** · 🔥 `quantum optics experiment` **4/5** · `Tavis-Cummings & cavity-many-emitter` **3/5**

**Summary.** The study achieves strong coupling between magnon modes and superconducting resonator photons in micron-scale YIG structures. By using FIB-milled microplatelets, the researchers overcame previous thickness limitations, enabling efficient, low-power magnonic-based quantum devices. This provides a foundation for on-chip studies of numerous long-lived excitations.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant to quantum optics and open quantum systems as it demonstrates a platform for scalable, on-chip strong coupling between bosonic excitations (magnons and photons) at extremely low power levels, which is a key requirement for hybrid quantum architectures.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Achieving strong coupling between magnons and microwave photons in sub-10 micron Yttrium Iron Garnet (YIG) structures has been difficult due to insufficient mode volume caused by YIG thickness limitations.

**Main result.** The researchers demonstrated strong coupling between numerous magnon modes in a YIG microplatelet and a superconducting LC resonator, even at extremely low input powers (<= 10 fW).

**Method.** The team used focused ion beam (FIB) techniques to create a YIG microplatelet from a single crystal and placed it on a constricted inductive line of an optimized superconducting lumped element LC resonator.

**Model / system.** The system consists of a micron-scale YIG microplatelet coupled to a superconducting lumped element LC resonator, involving the interaction between magnonic modes and resonator photons.

**Key observables.** Microwave transmission signal and anti-crossings in the transmission spectrum.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Sub-10 micron YIG structures, device input powers <= 10 fW.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the challenge of small-scale magnonics, describes the FIB fabrication of YIG microplatelets, presents experimental evidence of strong coupling via anti-crossings, validates results with micromagnetic simulations and analytical calculations, and demonstrates low-power operation.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Strong-coupling experiments based on magnons enable the exploration into on-chip demonstrations involving numerous long-lived excitations. Yttrium iron garnet (YIG) has been considered for decades as a gold standard material for magnonics due to its low-loss magnonic properties. While YIG has successfully demonstrated strong-coupling in macroscopic device geometries, the strong coupling of magnons in truly sub-10 micron YIG structures to date has not yet been realized. This obstacle is due to the difficulty producing large enough effective magnonic mode volume necessary primarily due to thickness limitations of YIG deposition and device fabrication techniques. Here, we demonstrate the use of a microplatelet of YIG, manufactured from a single crystal of YIG via focused ion beam (FIB) techniques, placed on a constricted inductive line of an optimized superconducting lumped element LC resonator to achieve strong coupling between numerous magnon modes and the LC resonator photons. These experimental findings are qualitatively backed by micromagnetic simulations and quantitatively supported by analytical calculations to identify the magnon modes corresponding to the experimentally observed anti-crossings in the microwave transmission signal. Further, we show that these anti-crossings remain even at incredibly low device input powers ($\leq 10$ fW). The fabrication techniques and device geometry enable the deterministic use of numerous confined magnon modes in micron-scale YIG structures for various magnetic field strengths and orientations at substantially reduced device powers. The results here establish a foundational path forward to achieving efficient magnon-based strong-coupling experiments in micron-scale YIG magnetic elements for effective on-chip studies.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27843"></a>
### [Spin-coherence characterization of boron vacancy defects in hexagonal boron nitride with broadband microwave pulses](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27843v1)

**Authors:** Yuki Nakamura, Takuya Iwasaki, Shu Nakaharai, Shinichi Ogawa, Yukinori Morita, Kenji Watanabe, Takashi Taniguchi, Kento Sasaki, Kensuke Kobayashi  
**Type:** experiment · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27843v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `QC/QI experiment` **4/5** · `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5** · `quantum optics experiment` **2/5**

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates a method to characterize the spin coherence of boron vacancy defects in hBN using broadband microwave pulses. By measuring T2* and T2 times, the study provides essential data for evaluating these defects as platforms for nanoscale quantum sensing. The approach is particularly useful for van der Waals thin films with broad resonance linewidths.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is relevant to researchers in open quantum systems and quantum optics as it provides experimental methods for characterizing decoherence and spin dynamics in solid-state defects used for quantum sensing.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Characterizing the spin coherence times (T2* and T2) of negatively charged boron vacancy (VB-) defects in hBN for use in nanoscale quantum sensing.

**Main result.** The study achieved sub-GHz Rabi oscillations and measured spin coherence times of T2* = 13.8 ns and T2 = 108.7 ns using broadband microwave pulses.

**Method.** The researchers used broadband microwave pulses on an isotopically enriched hBN thin film stamped onto a gold wire to perform Ramsey interference and Hahn echo measurements.

**Model / system.** The physical system consists of negatively charged boron vacancy (VB-) defects in an isotopically enriched hexagonal boron nitride (hBN) thin film placed on a narrow gold wire.

**Key observables.** Rabi oscillations, Ramsey interference signal decay, Hahn echo signal decay, and the stretch factor alpha.

**Important parameters / regimes.** T2* = 13.8 ns, T2 = 108.7 ns, and a stretch factor alpha = 1.25.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the potential of VB- defects for sensing, describes the experimental setup using gold wires and broadband pulses, presents the results of Ramsey and Hahn echo measurements, and concludes with the implications for evaluating spin defects in van der Waals materials.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Negatively charged boron vacancy (VB-) defects in hexagonal boron nitride (hBN) are promising for nanoscale-proximity quantum sensing. To evaluate their performance, it is important to characterize the spin coherence times T2* and T2. In this study, we realized sub-GHz Rabi oscillations of VB- using an isotopically enriched hBN thin film directly stamped onto a narrow gold wire. Using these strong microwave pulses, we performed Ramsey interference and Hahn echo measurements. The Ramsey interference signal showed Gaussian-like decay, yielding T2* = 13.8 ns. The Hahn echo measurement gave T2 = 108.7 ns and a stretch factor of α= 1.25. These results experimentally clarify the spin coherence properties of VB- and provide an effective method for evaluating the coherence of spin defects in van der Waals thin films with broad resonance linewidths.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27417"></a>
### [Mobile Exceptional Points Generate Momentum-Space Switching Domains](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27417v1)

**Authors:** Jung-Wan Ryu, Chang-Hwan Yi  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27417v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** `driven-dissipative phase transition` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `correlated / nonlocal dissipation` **2/5**

**Summary.** The paper shows that when exceptional points move during cyclic modulation, they create distinct regions in the Brillouin zone where bands switch or do not switch. This discovery provides a new method for controlling band topology in non-Hermitian systems, such as lossy photonic crystals.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for researchers in quantum optics and open quantum systems as it demonstrates a new way to engineer non-Hermitian topological phenomena by controlling the motion of exceptional points.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study investigates how the mobility of exceptional points (EPs) under cyclic modulation affects the band topology and creates new momentum-space structures.

**Main result.** Mobile EPs generate momentum-space switching domains that partition the Brillouin zone into regions with different band-switching behaviors, leading to global band switching at high modulation strengths.

**Method.** The authors use a minimal two-band lattice model to introduce a band-permutation invariant and demonstrate the effect in a photonic crystal with lossy materials.

**Model / system.** A minimal two-band lattice model under cyclic modulation and a photonic crystal platform incorporating lossy materials.

**Key observables.** Band-switching behavior, band-permutation invariant, and EP trajectories in extended parameter space.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Modulation strength, crystal momentum, and the modulation parameter.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the concept of mobile EPs, presents a theoretical framework using a two-band lattice model and a new band-permutation invariant, describes the formation of switching domains, and validates the predictions using a photonic crystal system.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Exceptional points (EPs), non-Hermitian degeneracies where both eigenvalues and eigenvectors coalesce, play a central role in the topology of non-Hermitian spectra. Recent advances have enabled the controlled creation and manipulation of EPs in a wide range of physical systems, raising the question of what new band topology emerges when EPs become mobile under cyclic modulation. Here we show that mobile EPs generate momentum-space switching domains that partition the Brillouin zone into regions with distinct band-switching behavior. Using a minimal two-band lattice model, we introduce a band-permutation invariant that determines whether eigenmodes exchange after one modulation cycle. The boundaries between switching regions arise from the projection of EP trajectories in an extended parameter space combining crystal momentum and the modulation parameter. As the modulation strength increases, the switching domains expand and eventually cover the entire Brillouin zone, resulting in global band switching. The predicted switching-domain structure is further demonstrated in a photonic crystal with lossy materials. These results open a new avenue within non-Hermitian topology by enabling the engineering of EP-driven phenomena through their controlled motion.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27611"></a>
### [Directional Cluster Migration Driven by Escape-Rate Asymmetry in Multi-Compartment Granular Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27611v1)

**Authors:** Kai Kono, Hiroyuki Ebata, Shio Inagaki  
**Type:** both · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27611v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **2/5**

**Summary.** The paper investigates how particle clusters move directionally between compartments in a vibrated granular system. By measuring species-specific fluxes, the authors show that an asymmetry in how small and large particles interact drives this migration. This work provides an experimental basis for modeling collective transport in driven, dissipative systems.

**Why it may be interesting.** The discovery of asymmetric, population-dependent flux and directional transport in a non-equilibrium system provides insights into collective transport and driven-dissipative dynamics relevant to open quantum systems.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Understanding the mechanism behind the directional stepwise migration of particle clusters in a multi-compartment vibrated granular system.

**Main result.** The study identifies an asymmetric interaction between particle species where large particles enhance small particle flux, while small particles suppress large particle flux, driving directional transport.

**Method.** Direct measurement of particle species flux as a function of instantaneous populations, followed by the implementation of a minimal flux model.

**Model / system.** A vertically vibrated granular system composed of small and large particles distributed across multiple compartments.

**Key observables.** Flux of small and large particle species, particle populations per compartment, and directional migration dynamics.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Mechanical agitation (vibration), particle size distribution, and instantaneous particle populations.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is treated as an out-of-equilibrium system driven by energy dissipation through inelastic collisions and friction.

**Paper structure.** Introduction to granular out-of-equilibrium dynamics, experimental report on directional cluster migration, flux measurement analysis, and validation via a minimal flux model.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Granular materials are inherently out-of-equilibrium systems due to energy dissipation through inelastic collisions and friction. When driven by mechanical agitation such as vibration, they exhibit rich collective behaviors including segregation, clustering, and spontaneous oscillations. Here, we report directional stepwise migration of particle clusters from one compartment to the next in a vertically vibrated granular system composed of small and large particles. To clarify the underlying mechanism, we directly measured how the flux of both particle species depends on the instantaneous particle populations. The measurements reveal an asymmetric interaction between particle species: the flux of small particles is enhanced by the presence of large particles, whereas that of large particles is suppressed by small particles. A minimal flux model incorporating these measured fluxes reproduces the observed directional dynamics and provides an experimentally grounded framework for collective transport in vibrated granular systems.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

### [Mapping the Phase Diagram of the Vicsek Model with Machine Learning](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28167v1)

**Authors:** Grace T. Bai, Brandon B. Le  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** disordered systems and neural networks · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28167v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>

</div>

**Summary.** This paper presents a machine learning framework to automatically map the complex phase diagram of the Vicsek model. By combining K-Means clustering with neural networks, the authors can identify coexistence regions and interpolate phase boundaries in a 3D parameter space. This provides a systematic way to extract global phase behavior from sparse simulation data in active matter models.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Mapping and classifying the 3D phase structure (order, disorder, and coexistence) of the Vicsek model across a parameter space of noise, density, and velocity.

**Main result.** The authors developed an ML pipeline that achieves 0.92 classification accuracy, successfully resolving a narrow coexistence region and interpolating phase boundaries beyond the original simulation points.

**Method.** A two-step machine learning approach using K-Means clustering on dynamical observables for unsupervised phase labeling, followed by a supervised neural network classifier for parameter-to-phase mapping.

**Model / system.** The Vicsek model, an agent-based model of self-propelled particles in 2D that exhibits collective motion/flocking behavior.

**Key observables.** Order parameter (phi), Binder cumulant (G), and susceptibility (chi).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Noise level (eta), particle density (rho), and self-propulsion velocity (v0).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study assumes that the K-Means clustering of steady-state observables accurately represents the underlying physical phases and that weighted cross-entropy is sufficient to handle class imbalance.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows K-Means clustering in observable space and the resulting phase labels projected onto parameter space; Figure 2 provides a 3D visualization of the learned phase diagram; Figure 3 shows 2D slices of the phase diagram in the (eta, rho) plane at different v0 values.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the Vicsek model and the problem of phase mapping, describes the simulation and ML pipeline (unsupervised clustering followed by supervised classification), presents the resulting 3D phase diagrams and 2D slices, and concludes with discussion on limitations and future work.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

In this study, we use machine learning to classify and interpolate the phase structure of the Vicsek flocking model across the three-dimensional parameter space $(η,ρ,v_0)$. We construct a dataset of simulated parameter points and characterize each point using long-time dynamical observables. These observables are then used as inputs to a K-Means clustering procedure, which assigns each point to a disorder, order, or coexistence phase. Using these clustered labels, we train a neural-network classifier to learn the mapping from model parameters to phase behavior, achieving a classification accuracy of 0.92. The resulting phase map resolves a narrow coexistence region separating the ordered and disordered phases and extends the inferred phase boundaries beyond the originally sampled simulation points. More broadly, this approach provides a systematic way to convert sparse simulation data into a global phase diagram for collective-motion models.

</details>
